    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer6605437771854236688">Wedding baker Laurel McBane is surrounded by romance working at Vows wedding planning company with her best friends Parker, Emma, and Mac.   <span id="freeText6605437771854236688" style="display:none">Wedding baker Laurel McBane is surrounded by romance working at Vows wedding planning company with her best friends Parker, Emma, and Mac. But she's too low-key to appreciate all the luxuries that their clients seem to long for. What she does appreciate is a strong, intelligent man, a man just like Parker's older brother Delaney, on whom she's had a mega-crush since childhood. <br /><br />But some infatuations last longer than others, and Laurel is convinced that the Ivy League lawyer is still out of her reach. Plus, Del is too protective of Laurel to ever cross the line with her-or so she thinks. When Laurel's quicksilver moods get the better of her-leading to an angry, hot, all-together mind-blowing kiss with Del—she'll have to quiet the doubts in her mind to turn a moment of passion into forever...</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/74004138-heather-mcc"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1514609433i/74004138._UY100_CR3,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/74004138-heather-mcc">Heather McC</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It depends on what you are into. It's the third book in a series, and I recommend reading the first two first. If you are still interested, the book f<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It depends on what you are into. It's the third book in a series, and I recommend reading the first two first. If you are still interested, the book follows the typical rom-com pattern of the first two books. One of the female protagonists starts a relationship, there's an inevitable breakup/roadblock, and ultimately there's a reunion ending with a proposal. It's formulaic to a degree but relatively harmless. Quick side note: there are sex scenes in this book that get more graphic than the previous two.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2373264770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6180134872489972189">Let's face it, Addie's intervention didn't work and there is no stopping me now from finishing this crappy series.   <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176640571?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176640571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16186755707586542731">Fell far below my expectations.<br/><br/>I really had high hopes for this book given that the previous two installments of this series amazingly hit the mark for me. But sadly, as far as I can tell, there was not much of a romantic spark between Delaney and Laurel here. And frankly, if there had been any chemistry between them, it would have felt totally forced.<br/><br/>Nope. I wasn’t pleased.<br/><br/>The romance aspect fell flat in my opinion and the dialogue between Delaney and Laurel was slightly lackluster. However, I </span>
  <span id="freeText16186755707586542731" style="display:none">Fell far below my expectations.<br /><br />I really had high hopes for this book given that the previous two installments of this series amazingly hit the mark for me. But sadly, as far as I can tell, there was not much of a romantic spark between Delaney and Laurel here. And frankly, if there had been any chemistry between them, it would have felt totally forced.<br /><br />Nope. I wasn’t pleased.<br /><br />The romance aspect fell flat in my opinion and the dialogue between Delaney and Laurel was slightly lackluster. However, I absolutely enjoyed an unconditional love and true friendship between these four ladies. Besides, the two couples from book 1 and 2 were so lovely that I couldn’t stop smiling and I was very happy to see them together again.<br /><br />The most disappointing part about this book was ‘Laurel’, and this fact came as a shock to me. Since I started reading this series, I saw no sign that she could be such an unpleasant character to read about. But when I finally got to her own story, I found that she managed to annoy and bore me in equal measure. I don’t like this kind of heroine at all. For me, she came across more like a bitter, sullen, and difficult woman. I don’t know. Something about her rubbed me the wrong way most of the time and I have to say that I didn’t enjoy her character throughout the entire story.<br /><br />Delaney was an ok hero but there was nothing particularly remarkable about him. Of course, he was nice but the fact that he couldn’t make me swoon over him says quite a lot about his character. It might be because he was somehow overshadowed by the other characters. I just wish there were more depth to his character.<br /><br />I felt like the ending was a bit rushed and unsatisfying. It could have been better though.<br /><br />This wasn’t a winner for me. To tell you the truth, reading this one felt more like a chore than a pleasure to get through.<br /><br />By the way, I’ll definitely read the last book in this Bride Quartet series. Hopefully, it won’t disappoint me like this one did!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16186755707586542731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3213049259731243485">3 1/2 stars<br/><br/>Once again, NR proves how good she is when it comes to write friendship. Unfortunately, that got in the way of the romance and I didn't connect with Del and Laurel's love story. Del was a nice guy, but too smooth and perfect to raise my temperature. Laurel was a bit harsher than him, but her bouts of temper felt forced to me because they were irrational and came out of nowhere. Okay, that is known to happen in Romancelandia, but that behavior is usually associated with a character who</span>
  <span id="freeText3213049259731243485" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars<br /><br />Once again, NR proves how good she is when it comes to write friendship. Unfortunately, that got in the way of the romance and I didn't connect with Del and Laurel's love story. Del was a nice guy, but too smooth and perfect to raise my temperature. Laurel was a bit harsher than him, but her bouts of temper felt forced to me because they were irrational and came out of nowhere. Okay, that is known to happen in Romancelandia, but that behavior is usually associated with a character who's also irrational - and that wasn't Laurel's case.<br /><br />So, all in all, this was a slightly better than average read to me, mostly because I enjoyed watching the friends' dynamics. Del and Laurel's romance was kind of meh. I was happy with their HEA, but I wouldn't be devastated if they had decided to stay just friends.<br /><br />Now I have a long wait until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7074000.Happy_Ever_After__Bride_Quartet___4_" title="Happy Ever After (Bride Quartet, #4) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Ever After</a>, the last book in the series. I really hope it's worth the wait and the series ends with a bang. :)<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103575692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1321315044918577620">2.5* This book is difficult to rate because I both liked it and didn't. It was an okay story overall, and I liked the characters, although I did get tired of Laurel at times. Mostly, though, I got stuck on the "snappy dialog" that made everyone sound like characters out of a TV sit com or Rom Com movie. Not only did everyone in the book respond with one or two word phrases, but everyone sounded identical. Even the older Mrs. Grady spoke mainly in predicates. Some of the dialog was funny and clev</span>
  <span id="freeText1321315044918577620" style="display:none">2.5* This book is difficult to rate because I both liked it and didn't. It was an okay story overall, and I liked the characters, although I did get tired of Laurel at times. Mostly, though, I got stuck on the "snappy dialog" that made everyone sound like characters out of a TV sit com or Rom Com movie. Not only did everyone in the book respond with one or two word phrases, but everyone sounded identical. Even the older Mrs. Grady spoke mainly in predicates. Some of the dialog was funny and clever, but it all sounded completely scripted, like the actors on a Disney channel tween show. So no matter how cute the story was, I was always completely distracted by dialog and the fact that no one talks that way in real life. (I know we don't talk in complete sentences all the time, but take a look at the book. Everyone answers in weird sentence fragments.) And, after 3 books, I'm over the "heart-warming groups of loyal best girlfriends." I started to feel a little gaggy at times. Everyone is so perfect and makes all these perfectly wonderful decisions.<br /><br />I also got tired of the repeated descriptions of the characters workouts. I can maybe see describing the cakes, or flowers, but Parker's exercise routine? (and Laurel's, and Mac's, and Mal's, for goodness sakes!) </span>
  <a data-text-id="1321315044918577620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_147528550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147528550" />
    <a title="Mojca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca"><img alt="Mojca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379576265p2/1359426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147528550?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mojca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mojca" href="/user/show/1359426-mojca">Mojca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=nora-roberts-jd-robb">nora-roberts-jd-robb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1359426-mojca?shelf=romantic-comedy-lol">romantic-comedy-lol</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147528550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3766457954942228345">And yet another <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a> winner in this amazing series. And this time, though it still revolved around the friendship between Mac, Emma, Laurel and Parker, the story was mostly about the romance between life-long friends. Yes, you’d think it was pretty much the same as in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6070950.Bed_of_Roses__Bride_Quartet___2_' title='Bed of Roses (Bride Quartet, #2) by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bed of Roses</a>, between Emma and Jack, but the thing is, Laurel and Del, Parker’s older brother have known (and been friends) each other for her entire life. So the switch held much more danger and possible obstacles. For the</span>
  <span id="freeText3766457954942228345" style="display:none">And yet another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a> winner in this amazing series. And this time, though it still revolved around the friendship between Mac, Emma, Laurel and Parker, the story was mostly about the romance between life-long friends. Yes, you’d think it was pretty much the same as in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6070950.Bed_of_Roses__Bride_Quartet___2_" title="Bed of Roses (Bride Quartet, #2) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Bed of Roses</a>, between Emma and Jack, but the thing is, Laurel and Del, Parker’s older brother have known (and been friends) each other for her entire life. So the switch held much more danger and possible obstacles. For them both, but mostly inside their little “tribe”.<br />So the same fears and worries as with Emma and Jack were there, but much more augmented, <i>because</i> of that long(er) friendship.<br /><br />But it was beautifully done, if you ask me, much better than in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6070950.Bed_of_Roses__Bride_Quartet___2_" title="Bed of Roses (Bride Quartet, #2) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Bed of Roses</a>, especially since the hero (Del) had no obvious and well-known commitment issues Jack had. He was much more laid back and relaxed when it came to his “thing” with Laurel and he had no compunction in stating his love for her, since everybody knew he loved her. Pity, that, since the words held no “special meaning” being said so many times before, no wonder she was skeptical and a little skittish.<br />And that is the biggest problem I had with Laurel. It didn’t overly bother me, since I understood her reservations, but still, sometimes she came off as a bit too impulsive in her judgment. And too stubborn to listen...or talk about what bothered her. But, her love for Del was there, and I forgave her. ;)<br /><br />Now, onto the less-friendship-more-romance thingy. Well, it’s true. Sure, the girls were still tight as ever, they talked, they laughed, they cried, they ribbed each other, but there was that much appreciated lack of “friendly intervention” at the end, that was present in both previous novels, and an especial “burden” in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6070950.Bed_of_Roses__Bride_Quartet___2_" title="Bed of Roses (Bride Quartet, #2) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Bed of Roses</a>. First, it was because Laurel was more reserved by nature, preferring to solve her problems on her own and second, there was no big rift between her and Del to demand an intervention in the first place. Sure, she made a mess with her stubbornness and refusal to listen, but it was quickly resolved.<br />And who resolved it? Del, of course. Who’s become my favorite hero in this series a few pages into this story. Who wouldn’t want a guy like Del? Who wouldn’t love a guy like Del? He was (over)protective, self-assured, caring, loving, tender, funny, sexy (my mouth watered reading the pond scene), and romantic (the awwwwww-factor in the ending was all him).<br />I love my girls (the Quartet) and I love Carter and Jack, but Del is by far my favorite.<br /><br />I’m sure he’ll fall into second place today, as I start reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7840873.Happy_Ever_After__Bride_Quartet___4_" title="Happy Ever After (Bride Quartet, #4) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Ever After</a>, because there’s just something about Malcolm Kavanaugh that “inspires” me. I cannot wait to read about him and Parker. If the sparkage these two produced in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7076717.Savor_the_Moment__Bride_Quartet___3_" title="Savor the Moment (Bride Quartet, #3) by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Savor the Moment</a> is any indication, the fireworks will go through the roof when it’s their turn. Can’t wait! *happy squeal*<br /><br />Well, this series is shaping to be my favorite (short) series I’ve read in my life. Romantic, funny, sexy, sensual, light-weight, emotion-engaging...A truly awesome read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3766457954942228345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer13926036397831426574">This is probably my least favorite installment into this series and my least favorite couple, and I still really enjoy both the book and the couple. Doesn’t that speak volumes of my love for the series?<br/><br/>Laurel is an amazing pastry chef. The wedding cakes she designs for her clients are beautiful enough to make angels weep, and are always lovingly personalized to each couple. Parker has been her best friend for as long as she can remember, and she’s been in love with Parker’s older brother for alm</span>
  <span id="freeText13926036397831426574" style="display:none">This is probably my least favorite installment into this series and my least favorite couple, and I still really enjoy both the book and the couple. Doesn’t that speak volumes of my love for the series?<br /><br />Laurel is an amazing pastry chef. The wedding cakes she designs for her clients are beautiful enough to make angels weep, and are always lovingly personalized to each couple. Parker has been her best friend for as long as she can remember, and she’s been in love with Parker’s older brother for almost as long. Delaney has always viewed Laurel as another sister; or at least, he did, until she completely destroyed that viewpoint by kissing the sisterly affection right out of him. The relationship they build from the ashes of that familial fondness is sweet and funny.<br /><br />Laurel is incredibly sarcastic, and not the most optimistic of women. Her surliness is at odds with her sunny blonde hair and cornflower blue eyes. She’s super entertaining, but I just don’t connect quite as much with her as I do with the other three women that form the Quartet. Same goes for Del. He’s a slick lawyer with a propensity for micromanaging the lives of those he loves, which drives Laurel insane. But he’s also incredibly kind and chivalrous, so it’s hard to hold that against him. But again, I just don’t connect as much to him as I do to the other three men who fall in love with various members of the Quartet. <br /><br />All of that being said, I still devoured this book (cake pun intended). When the weakest volume of a series is still 4 stars, you know it’s a favorite.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15497373668023666913">I love the way Nora Roberts crafts her characters. You're sure to fall in love with them while they fall in love with each other. <br/>This third installment of The Bride Quartet doesn't disappoint in any way. Del and Laurel verbally spar with each other and the dialogue snaps as you'll laugh at their witty comebacks at one another.<br/>While Mac and Carter continue to be my favorite couple of this series, this comes a very close second.<br/>Laurel is one tough cookie, to use a baking analogy, and she has love</span>
  <span id="freeText15497373668023666913" style="display:none">I love the way Nora Roberts crafts her characters. You're sure to fall in love with them while they fall in love with each other. <br />This third installment of The Bride Quartet doesn't disappoint in any way. Del and Laurel verbally spar with each other and the dialogue snaps as you'll laugh at their witty comebacks at one another.<br />While Mac and Carter continue to be my favorite couple of this series, this comes a very close second.<br />Laurel is one tough cookie, to use a baking analogy, and she has loved Del all her life, finally she decides to do something about it. In comic retaliation, Del steals her shoes(you'll have to read it to understand all of this).<br />The love story is wonderful, but what makes this series so enjoyable is the four friends and the relationship they all have and the friendships between the men in their lives as they get to know one another. The scenes where the four women are together, discussing everything from weddings, their own as well as others, to their love lives, troublesome parents, etc are often laugh out loud funny. <br />One last thing, I love all the initial-speak that the girls do together and in this book, you'll learn a new one: HJS.<br />Oh, and even though we aren't yet to his story, I'm already a teeny bit in lurve with Mal. Can't wait for the final book.</span>

<div id="review_78065259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78065259" />
    <a title="Miss Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/925549-miss-kim"><img alt="Miss Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369060240p2/925549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78065259?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miss Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miss Kim" href="/user/show/925549-miss-kim">Miss Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925549-miss-kim?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78065259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17637681526924471300">3 1/2 stars<br/><br/>*sigh*. I really wanted to love this one, but I didn't. I did like Del and Lauren, but I didn't like the 'conflict'. It was weak, since she'd known him her whole life. It felt like the author had to come up with something to make them 'have it out' before they got an HEA. I am so looking forward to Parker and Mal's book. We get to visit them a bit and this one, and I kept wishing for this to be their book. Ah well, we can't love em all.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

She thinks that they all talk about hot jungle sex (and refer to it as HJS - puh-leeze) and call each other bitches. <br /><br />It was an okay story, but you really aren't missing anything if you skip this one. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11095815487114623754">Unless the next one really pulls out all the stops, this will probably remain my favourite of the series. <br/><br/>I didn't know what to expect from Laurel, because in the previous books she'd always seemed like the kind of character I neither like nor dislike. She was also known by the others as the hard-ass of the group, together with Parker, so I didn't know what I'd be in </span>
  <span id="freeText11095815487114623754" style="display:none">Unless the next one really pulls out all the stops, this will probably remain my favourite of the series. <br /><br />I didn't know what to expect from Laurel, because in the previous books she'd always seemed like the kind of character I neither like nor dislike. She came across as vaguely annoyed and somewhat ill-tempered all the time, but not necessarily in a bad way, if that makes sense. She was also known by the others as the hard-ass of the group, together with Parker, so I didn't know what I'd be in for with this book.<br /><br />Del, on the other hand, I pretty much loved from the very first mention of him in book 1. And I liked them together a lot, even though the whole unrequited crush trope can be tricky sometimes. Their banter and sarcastic comments thrown back-and-forth especially worked for me. Plus, there was little to no conflict here and what <i>was</i> there made sense. Laurel had a dumb meltdown moment towards the end, but then I'd come to expect that with these books. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_103848114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103848114" />
    <a title="K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2592043-k"><img alt="K." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350796767p2/2592043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103848114?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="K." href="/user/show/2592043-k">K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2592043-k?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103848114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1755711323163198790">I've been pretty eager for this book to come out, as I've been happily following the series. Surprising for me how much I've enjoyed this new series by Nora Roberts since I'm not usually a big fan of her books (hit and miss with me). I suspect part of the reason I'm particularly attracted to the stories is due to the wedding planner theme -- it's particularly girly, and I'm pretty darn "girly" myself! ;) Also love the life-long friends falling in love with guys who've been their life-long friend</span>
  <span id="freeText1755711323163198790" style="display:none">I've been pretty eager for this book to come out, as I've been happily following the series. Surprising for me how much I've enjoyed this new series by Nora Roberts since I'm not usually a big fan of her books (hit and miss with me). I suspect part of the reason I'm particularly attracted to the stories is due to the wedding planner theme -- it's particularly girly, and I'm pretty darn "girly" myself! ;) Also love the life-long friends falling in love with guys who've been their life-long friends as well. Girl-next store falls in love with boy-next door stuff - another "girly" type romance theme. Anyway ...<br /><br />I enjoyed Laurel and Del's story immensely. BUT ... I have a feeling these books may come off better in audio than they might be in paper book form. Angela Dawe is the reader on this one, and she's spectacular. She gives a lot of life to the characters, and her inflection and emotion is spot on. Her voices are distinct, and match the characters she assigns them to. I really "get" her emotional vibes, and that goes a long way in getting into the scenes. <br /><br />Laurel and Del have been virtually life-long friends, and have even "married each other a couple of times" by the time they'd grown up. Since the 4 main heroines of this series own a very successful wedding planning business, Parker (Del's sister) had collared Del a few times to "play groom" by the time he was 8 or 9 years old and paired him up with best friend Laurel while playing "bride" together. Laurel, however, has always known she's hopelessly in love with Del, and that no matter how often she's tried to change the fact and refocus her energies toward other relationships, Del's "THE one" for her! Del has a harder time defining his feelings for Laurel, although he's never doubted for a moment he "love's" her, and has always loved her ... that "love" wasn't the kind typically assigned to a "lover." However, he too has shocked himself a couple of times by how attracted he's begun to find Laurel, and he's a bit afraid of how that sexual attraction might mess up their life-long friendship, which means a lot to him. <br /><br />I've heard a few reviewers define Laurel's attitude as a bit too bitchy toward Del, and that just doesn't come across in the audiobook. The narrator makes her feelings appropriate and I always knew that Laurel was just "guarding" her feelings. Del comes across as the "head of the family" (which encompasses ALL of his circle of friends, including Laurel): Very in-charge, protective, yet funny and cool type of guy. Their road to figuring out their relationship/love for each other brings the series to a nice conclusion for Laurel/Del, and includes enough set up for Parker and Mal's forthcoming book. Can't wait! The whole audiobook series is worth listening to more than once. <br />K.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1755711323163198790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <td colspan="2">

  <span id="freeText7154358498455358005" style="display:none">Unfortunately, this one was just ok for me. I was kind of bored with both Del and Laurel. If Laurel loved Del her whole life I didn't see much of it. I really got tired of all the exercise and scenes with the brides that really didn't have anything to do with the Del and Laurel. I guess I wanted to see them together more and it just didn't happen.<br /><br />I kind of trudged through this one and was glad it was finally over. It's not to say I didn't enjoy parts of the book but for the most part this book was boring for me. In my books I like to have a little conflict between the H/h and they just came together. Yes, Laurel loved Del forever but it didn't feel real to me. It seemed there was more focus on exercise, baking, weddings and the four friends. Friendships are wonderful of course, but this is a romance. I wanted a bit more. It all fell flat for me.<br /><br />I definitely liked Jack and Emma's story better. I hope I enjoy Malcolm and Parker's story.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer920970647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17765168303798500810"><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>Sometimes we read a book that is not only good, it also turns out to be perfect for the current mood were in.<br/>That's what happened with this one. A perfect read for a relaxed Saturday afternoon.<br/> <br/>I guess by now, there isn't much more I can say about Nora Roberts' writing:<br/>The author definitely knows how to spin a tale. If you've already read some of the author's books, you know what I'm talking about. If not....well, your loss...<br/> <br/>So in this story _once again _ we have some smooth, flowing writi</span>
  <span id="freeText17765168303798500810" style="display:none"><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Sometimes we read a book that is not only good, it also turns out to be perfect for the current mood were in.<br>That's what happened with this one. A perfect read for a relaxed Saturday afternoon.<br> <br>I guess by now, there isn't much more I can say about Nora Roberts' writing:<br>The author definitely knows how to spin a tale. If you've already read some of the author's books, you know what I'm talking about. If not....well, your loss...<br> <br>So in this story _once again _ we have some smooth, flowing writing, and the rest it's basically up to us readers:<br>Which are our favourite characters?<br>With whom do we identify the most? Which pair pulls at our heart strings?<br>Myself....I liked the first book VISION IN WHITE. There was a little too much talking about weddings _ I KNOW! The SHOCK! lol_ but I loved the main couple. Especially Carter who is such a sweetie.<br> <br>The second one not so much, mainly because of the last part who derailed a little on the drama department...but I'm happy to report _from the romance front_ that this one was another winner!<br> <br>In terms of conflict, _at a soap opera level_, don't expect it to happen here (Thank God!).<br> <br>Nora Roberts knows how to play the dynamics between friends, family and lovers, in such a way, that most of the times, I can't help feeling that I know these people.<br> <br>This is Laurel's, _ the pastries' chef book and Del, Parker's brother.<br>There isn't much to say about this story, besides it being a sweet romance.<br> <br>Myself I loved it, because the romance was the focus of it. And I especially enjoyed it due to the lack of dramatics (other people will say that it was boring, and that it just lacked tension and conflict. As we know, Tastes are Tastes..).<br> <br>The characters feel real, and most importantly, mentally healthy!<br>There's no screamings, and bouts of jealousy going around. <br><br>Instead there's just normal people, with normal insecurities trying to make a relationship work.<br>Then there was also some occasional funny and awe inducing moments.<br>Like this one:<br> <br>Feeling foolish, Laurel opened the envelope. <i>You might think this is over, but you’d be wrong. <b>I’ve taken your shoes hostage. Contact me within forty-eight hours, or the Pradas get it.</b></i><br><br>Author Official Site<br> <br>Buy "Savour The Moment"<br>@Bookdepository.com</span>

<div id="review_2229607946" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2229607946?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2229607946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6280002839013936178">This ended up being my highest rated book out of the Bride Quartet series. Probably cause of the mess that Emma and the crew did in book #2 ended up annoying the crap out of me. This one was a really great slow burning romance that thank God had none of the drama of the second book.<br/><br/>Book #3 is about Laurel. Laurel is the baker for the wedding planning business. She ends up getting involved with Del (Parker's brother) and feels out of sorts about how their "relationship" came about and what it eve</span>
  <span id="freeText6280002839013936178" style="display:none">This ended up being my highest rated book out of the Bride Quartet series. Probably cause of the mess that Emma and the crew did in book #2 ended up annoying the crap out of me. This one was a really great slow burning romance that thank God had none of the drama of the second book.<br /><br />Book #3 is about Laurel. Laurel is the baker for the wedding planning business. She ends up getting involved with Del (Parker's brother) and feels out of sorts about how their "relationship" came about and what it even means. Laurel is stubborn about things, but I liked her a lot. She was snarly and combative with her love interest, but it was a nice change of pace. <br /><br />Del has been a long time fan of all of the "girls". Del at times you got to see was overly protective of all of the women in the series, and though it was a little much at times, it wasn't offputting. He honestly reminded me of Josh Templeton from the "Daring to Dream" series. I liked that he didn't let Laurel push him away and listened to her and made sure she listened to him. <br /><br />Reading about people working out is boring. Seriously. I could not believe that Roberts included scenes of that. I didn't care about Mac working out to look nice in her wedding dress. I just rolled my eyes. The wedding scenes at this point are here to stay along with the acronyms galore. I honestly just rolled my eyes at how all of the heroes in this series who have full time jobs by the way, happen to always be around to help out the women. It's like how Roarke is always running after Eve like he doesn't have a full time job dealing with a million things. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6280002839013936178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127466652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127466652" />
    <a title="Aly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3528600-aly"><img alt="Aly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497047496p2/3528600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127466652?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly" href="/user/show/3528600-aly">Aly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127466652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4906237707284444617">Laurel is the total opposite of Emma who dreamed about romance and Prince Charming. She didn't understand the hype and the dramatic outburst that love can bring. She's more serious, discreet and in her head than the other three. I can't decide which heroine I liked best between her and Mac. I liked them for different reasons so it's difficult to make a choice. <br/><br/>Laurel didn't have the best nor the worst childhood. Her parents were often absent and didn't have lot of money so it's only thanks to Mr</span>
  <span id="freeText4906237707284444617" style="display:none">Laurel is the total opposite of Emma who dreamed about romance and Prince Charming. She didn't understand the hype and the dramatic outburst that love can bring. She's more serious, discreet and in her head than the other three. I can't decide which heroine I liked best between her and Mac. I liked them for different reasons so it's difficult to make a choice. <br /><br />Laurel didn't have the best nor the worst childhood. Her parents were often absent and didn't have lot of money so it's only thanks to Mrs. G, the Brown's housekeeper and an other mother figure to the girls, who paid for her tuitions, that she could go to Culinary Institute in New York. <br /><br />Laurel create cake for the brides. Delaney Brown is a lawyer and the legal advisor of Vow's. He and Laurel have known each other all their life and Laurel always had a crush on him. She never told a thing because she's not a go-getter or the kind of girl who take risks. Anyway, Del treated her too much like a friend and a member of his clan. Del is smooth and loyal but his protective side can sometimes makes him appear as a "know it all." For Del and Laurel, irritation is just an other word for attraction.<br /><br />I have a weakness for brother's best friend trope. I can't say the way things were handled in this one made it the most satisfying that I read. In fact, both Del and Laurel were so stubborn that their romance began almost like a competition. After a kiss that changed the way Del see Laurel, he propose an arrangement : for a month, they'll date and see where the new dynamic could leads them, and sex must be out of the equation to not muddy the waters. For me, it seemed kind of unromantic and anticlimatic. As if they were thinking, well, since half of our friends found love, what not try it. I expected more fireworks between Laurel and Del and I didn't feel the passion. <br /><br />This series made me notice something about Nora Roberts's writing style. It's a mix of old-fashioned romance, something merry or whimsical and a no-nonsense rational way of thinking and talking. <br /><br />This series is as much about friendship as romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4906237707284444617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345555230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2218509926636841339">Laurel is the baker of cakes and fine pastries for Vows and the mean one of the group of friends. Fierce about her friends, she doesn't hesitate to rip up at anybody who threatens those she loves. She has been a source of constant pressure on Mac and Emma's suitors in the first two books of this series, so I was interested what would happen when it was time for her to fall herself. Short answer: fun ride, though about as tense as you might expect.<br/><br/>Since she has been secretly in love with Parker's</span>
  <span id="freeText2218509926636841339" style="display:none">Laurel is the baker of cakes and fine pastries for Vows and the mean one of the group of friends. Fierce about her friends, she doesn't hesitate to rip up at anybody who threatens those she loves. She has been a source of constant pressure on Mac and Emma's suitors in the first two books of this series, so I was interested what would happen when it was time for her to fall herself. Short answer: fun ride, though about as tense as you might expect.<br /><br />Since she has been secretly in love with Parker's brother Del since, well, practically forever, you just know that things are going to be awkward. Del has taken a big-brother role with all of the girls and protected them when he could and helped them as often as they'd let him since they were kids. Independent since the death of his parents years ago, he has become a successful lawyer, acknowledged business leader, and is a silent partner in Vows. So when Laurel is provoked by his brotherly protectiveness into laying a steamy kiss on him, things get very interesting, fast.<br /><br />I was really glad that this book didn't go with a <u>Taming of the Shrew</u> farce motif. It could easily have done so. Instead, we get to see the vulnerability at Laurel's core and Del's need to be with someone who will challenge him as deeply as she loves him. And I particularly liked that Del got to show his own devious streak while he was at it.<br /><br />This book was a bit more scattered than the previous two with storyline deviations and longer alternate viewpoints. Most of this is obvious setup for Parkers coming turn in the hot-seat, but some was simply character establishment for Del. He's been at the fringes of the other books enough that I thought those deviations unnecessary, though not intrusively so. While a weaker story than the others, I still found it emotionally satisfying and loved the eventual resolution.<br /><br /><strong>A note on Steamy</strong>: This book is solidly mid-level steamy. It had what I'm coming to consider the Roberts Standard—two explicit sex scenes that go generic before becoming uncomfortably graphic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2218509926636841339" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15433558693465119770">This review contains at least two spoilers<br/><br/><br/>I really liked this book and can't wait for the next one coming in November. I'm actually hoping Nora Roberts decides to do at least one book about them all having kids that like the girls all grow up together. There was however one thing that bugged me and it has to do with logistics. At one point all the main characters plan to spend the day together (July 4th to be exact) then all go out drinking and dancing that night. They choose Carter to be Design</span>
  <span id="freeText15433558693465119770" style="display:none">This review contains at least two spoilers<br /><br /><br />I really liked this book and can't wait for the next one coming in November. I'm actually hoping Nora Roberts decides to do at least one book about them all having kids that like the girls all grow up together. There was however one thing that bugged me and it has to do with logistics. At one point all the main characters plan to spend the day together (July 4th to be exact) then all go out drinking and dancing that night. They choose Carter to be Designated Driver. The night before since they all plan to go together Del spends the night at Parker and Laurel's. On July 4th after they leave the nightclub Carter takes Del home. Laurel later jumps out of the van and runs to Del's. In the morning Del drives Laurel home. Here's the logistic problem. Wouldn't Del's car be at Laurel's house? I get the whole part about Laurel giving into temptation and running to Del's so in a matter of speaking he had to be dropped off at his house for a certain event to occur. Course she could have just visited his room when they got back to her house and although not as dramatic could have been just as good or even better. The other thing didn't really bug me I just kept waiting for it to happen but it never did. Del tells Jack that he has had feelings for Laurel but always believed her to be hands off so that's what he's done. I kept waiting for him to tell Laurel that but he never does. I think he may have implied it at the end but he never actually tells her that. I have this whole additional dialog in my head where he tells her about the whole believing it had to be hands off but it changed that night on the stairs and that when they were kids he objected to being Groom to all of them but when it was her he really didn't mind at all. Course I'm not Nora Roberts so...</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102127726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11092570868929158007">Mackenzie, Parker, Laurel and Emmaline have been friends since childhood and have formed a successful wedding planning business together called Vows. Although they help thousands of couples organise their biggest day, all have been unlucky in love. Until now<br/><br/>Laurel’s been in love with Del all her life but he just sees’s her as another one of the girls. Until Del pushes Laurel’s buttons too far and she kisses him.<br/>Let the games begin...<br/>When I first read the blurb for this story I thought it sounded</span>
  <span id="freeText11092570868929158007" style="display:none">Mackenzie, Parker, Laurel and Emmaline have been friends since childhood and have formed a successful wedding planning business together called Vows. Although they help thousands of couples organise their biggest day, all have been unlucky in love. Until now<br /><br />Laurel’s been in love with Del all her life but he just sees’s her as another one of the girls. Until Del pushes Laurel’s buttons too far and she kisses him.<br />Let the games begin...<br />When I first read the blurb for this story I thought it sounded a bit dull. But, really it’s not. In true Nora Roberts Style she gives us a lovely heart warming story of two people who have been friends all their lives, and fall deeply in love.<br />This story is about Laurel and Del finding their way from friends to lovers to a happy ever after.<br />This is not a story for people who like a good angst romance because this is a real love story. Laurel is a bit self conscious of herself when compared to Del, he came from money and loving parents, where she came from a broken home without her family supporting her. She put herself through college to live her dream of being a professional baker and loves what she does at Vows.<br /><br />Favourite Quote: Del’s note to Laurel “You might think this is over, but you’d be wrong. I’ve taken you shoes hostage. Contact me within forty-eight hours, or the Pradas get it.”<br /></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1863014515?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425233689" href="/book/show/7076717-savor-the-moment">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1863014515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5055522044667122443">Something about this didn't click with me. I think it's because I don't have a real handle on Laurel: she feels patched together from pieces of the other three women, and so she never becomes a person in her own right. It seems like she's just going through the motions - acting and reacting either the way you'd expect, or the way needed to drive the plot forward - and so I never lost sight of the fact (like I did in book 1!) that I was reading something. <br/><br/>Also, this is the point where the series </span>
  <span id="freeText5055522044667122443" style="display:none">Something about this didn't click with me. I think it's because I don't have a real handle on Laurel: she feels patched together from pieces of the other three women, and so she never becomes a person in her own right. It seems like she's just going through the motions - acting and reacting either the way you'd expect, or the way needed to drive the plot forward - and so I never lost sight of the fact (like I did in book 1!) that I was reading something. <br /><br />Also, this is the point where the series sags under its own weight. There are already two happy couples, and they're always being called out, and they all live in the same place and are together all the time... it's getting to be too much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5055522044667122443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rsRQ5smhQ3q2pD5/aVN4GcQMCHFyzKvX/9nyfbEY5kC5Hw9SWebwrVFLTv4cV5YqdsFwcEcCVb0tmaqNeaOvlg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
